MOLESWORTH\xe2\x80\x99S\r\n                         Stories for Children.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere is hardly a better author to put into the hands of children than\r\nMrs. Molesworth. I cannot easily speak too highly of her work. It is a\r\ncurious art she has, not wholly English in its spirit, but a cross of\r\nthe old English with the Italian. Indeed, I should say Mrs. Molesworth\r\nhad also been a close student of the German and Russian, and had some\r\nway, catching and holding the spirit of all, created a method and tone\r\nquite her own.... Her characters are admirable and real.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_St. Louis\r\nGlobe-Democrat._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth has a rare gift for composing stories for children.\r\nWith a light yet forcible touch, she paints sweet and artless, yet\r\nnatural and strong, characters.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Congregationalist._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth always has in her books those charming touches of\r\nnature that are sure to charm small people. Her stories are so likely to\r\nhave been true that men \xe2\x80\x98grown up\xe2\x80\x99 do not disdain them.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Home Journal._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo English writer of childish stories has a better reputation than Mrs.\r\nMolesworth, and none with whose stories we are familiar deserves it\r\nbetter. She has a motherly knowledge of the child nature, a clear sense\r\nof character, the power of inventing simple incidents that interest, and\r\nthe ease which comes of continuous practice.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Mail and Express._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cChristmas would hardly be Christmas without one of Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nstories. No one has quite the same power of throwing a charm and an\r\ninterest about the most commonplace every-day doings as she has, and no\r\none has ever blended fairy-land and reality with the same\r\nskill.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Educational Times._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth is justly a great favorite with children; her stories\r\nfor them are always charmingly interesting and healthful in\r\ntone.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Home Journal._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s books are cheery, wholesome, and particularly well\r\nadapted to refined life. It is safe to add that Mrs. Molesworth is the\r\nbest English prose writer for children.... A new volume from Mrs.\r\nMolesworth is always a treat.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_The Beacon._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo holiday season would be complete for a host of young readers without\r\na volume from the hand of Mrs. Molesworth.... Carrots and his sister are\r\ndelightful little beings, whom to read about is at once to become very\r\nfond of.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Examiner._\r\n\r\n\r\n              A CHRISTMAS CHILD; A Sketch of a Boy\xe2\x80\x99s Life.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA very sweet and tenderly drawn sketch, with life and reality manifest\r\nthroughout.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Pall Mall Gazette._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a capital story, well illustrated. Mrs. Molesworth is one of\r\nthose sunny, genial writers who has genius for writing acceptably for\r\nthe young. She has the happy faculty of blending enough real with\r\nromance to make her stories very practical for good without robbing them\r\nof any of their exciting interest.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Chicago Inter-Ocean._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth is one of the few writers of tales for children whose\r\nsentiment though of the sweetest kind is never sickly; whose religious\r\nfeeling is never concealed yet never obtruded; whose books are always\r\ngood but never \xe2\x80\x98goody.\xe2\x80\x99 Little Ted with his soft heart, clever head, and\r\nbrave spirit is no morbid presentment of the angelic child \xe2\x80\x98too good to\r\nlive,\xe2\x80\x99 and who is certainly a nuisance on earth, but a charming\r\ncreature, if not a portrait, whom it is a privilege to meet even in\r\nfiction.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_The Academy._\r\n\r\n\r\n                           THE CUCKOO CLOCK.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA beautiful little story.... It relates the\r\nadventures of two lovable English children lost in Paris, and is just\r\nwonderful enough to pleasantly wring the youthful heart.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_New York\r\nTribune._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is, in its way, indeed, a little classic, of which the real beauty\r\nand pathos can hardly be appreciated by young people.... It is not too\r\nmuch to say of the story that it is perfect of its kind.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Critic and\r\nGood Literature._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a charming little juvenile story from the pen of Mrs.\r\nMolesworth, detailing the various adventures of a couple of motherless\r\nchildren in searching for their father, whom they had missed in Paris,\r\nwhere they had gone to meet him.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Montreal Star._\r\n\r\n\r\n                           THE TAPESTRY ROOM.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth is the queen of children\xe2\x80\x99s fairy-land. She knows how to\r\nmake use of the vague, fresh, wondering instincts of childhood, and to\r\ninvest familiar things with fairy glamour.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Athen\xc3\xa6um._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe story told is a charming one of what may be called the neo-fairy\r\nsort.... There has been nothing better of its kind done anywhere for\r\nchildren, whether we consider its capacity to awaken interest or its\r\nwholesomeness.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Evening Post._\r\n\r\n\r\n                          CHRISTMAS-TREE LAND.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is conceived after a happy fancy, as it relates the supposititious\r\njourney of a party of little ones through that part of fairy-land where\r\nChristmas-trees are supposed to most abound. There is just enough of the\r\nold-fashioned fancy about fairies mingled with the \xe2\x80\x98modern improvements\xe2\x80\x99\r\nto incite and stimulate the youthful imagination to healthful action.\r\nThe pictures by Walter Crane are, of course, not only well executed in\r\nthemselves, but in charming consonance with the spirit of the\r\ntale.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Troy Times._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Christmas-Tree Land_, by Mrs. Molesworth, is a book to make younger\r\nreaders open their eyes wide with delight. A little boy and a little\r\ngirl, domiciled in a great white castle, wander on their holidays\r\nthrough the surrounding fir-forests, and meet with the most delightful\r\npleasures. There is a fascinating, mysterious character in their\r\nadventures and enough of the fairylike and wonderful to puzzle and\r\nenchant all the little ones.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Home Journal._\r\n\r\n\r\n                           A CHRISTMAS POSY.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a collection of eight of those inimitable stories for children\r\nwhich none could write better than Mrs. Molesworth. Her books are prime\r\nfavorites with children of all ages, and they are as good and wholesome\r\nas they are interesting and popular. This makes a very handsome book,\r\nand its illustrations are excellent.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Christian at Work._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_A Christmas Posy_, by Mrs. Molesworth, is lovely and fragrant. Mrs.\r\nMolesworth succeeds by right to the place occupied with so much honor by\r\nthe late Mrs. Ewing, as a writer of charming stories for children. The\r\npresent volume is a cluster of delightful short stories. Mr. Crane\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nillustrations are in harmony with the text.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Christian Intelligencer._\r\n\r\n\r\n                      THE CHILDREN OF THE CASTLE.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_The Children of the Castle_, by Mrs. Molesworth, is another of those\r\ndelightful juvenile stories of which this author has written so many. It\r\nis a fascinating little book, with a charming plot, a sweet, pure\r\natmosphere, and teaches a wholesome moral in the most winning\r\nmanner.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_B. S. E. Gazette._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_The Children of the Castle_ are delightful creations, actual little\r\ngirls, living in an actual castle, but often led by their fancies into a\r\nshadowy fairy-land. There is a charming refinement of style and spirit\r\nabout the story from beginning to end; an imaginative child will find\r\nendless pleasure in it, and the lesson of gentleness and unselfishness\r\nis so artistically managed that it does not seem like a lesson, but only\r\na part of the story.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Milwaukee Sentinel._\r\n\r\n\r\n                            FOUR WINDS FARM.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s books are always delightful, but of all none is more\r\ncharming than the volume with which she greets the holidays this season.\r\n_Four Winds Farm_ is one of the most delicate and pleasing books for a\r\nchild that has seen the light this many a day. It is full of fancy and\r\nof that instinctive sympathy with childhood which makes this author\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nbooks so attractive and so individual.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Courier._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStill more delicately fanciful is Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s lovely little tale\r\nof the _Four Winds Farm_. It is neither a dream nor a fairy story, but\r\nconcerns the fortune of a real little boy, named Gratian; yet the dream\r\nand the fairy tale seem to enter into his life, and make part of it. The\r\nfarmhouse in which the child lives is set exactly at the meeting-place\r\nof the four winds, and they, from the moment of his birth, have acted as\r\nhis self-elected godmothers.... All the winds love the boy, and, held in\r\nthe balance of their influence, he grows up as a boy should, simply and\r\ntruly, with a tender heart and firm mind. The idea of this little book\r\nis essentially poetical.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Literary World._\r\n\r\n\r\n                       NURSE HEATHERDALE\xe2\x80\x99S STORY.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Nurse Heatherdale\xe2\x80\x99s Story_ is all about a small boy, who was good\r\nenough, yet was always getting into some trouble through complications\r\nin which he was not to blame. The same sort of things happens to men and\r\nwomen. He is an orphan, though he is cared for in a way by relations,\r\nwho are not so very rich, yet are looked on as well fixed. After many\r\nyouthful trials and disappointments he falls into a big stroke of good\r\nluck, which lifts him and goes to make others happy. Those who want a\r\nchild\xe2\x80\x99s book will find nothing to harm and something to interest in this\r\nsimple story.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Commercial Advertiser._\r\n\r\n\r\n                                 \xe2\x80\x9cUS.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s _Us, an Old-Fashioned Story_, is very charming. A\r\ndear little six-year-old \xe2\x80\x98bruvver\xe2\x80\x99 and sister constitute the \xe2\x80\x98us,\xe2\x80\x99 whose\r\nadventures with gypsies form the theme of the story. Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nstyle is graceful, and she pictures the little ones with brightness and\r\ntenderness.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Evening Post._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA pretty and wholesome story.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Literary World._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Us, an Old-Fashioned Story_, is a sweet and quaint story of two little\r\nchildren who lived long ago, in an old-fashioned way, with their\r\ngrandparents. The story is delightfully told.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Philadelphia News._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Us_ is one of Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s charming little stories for young\r\nchildren. The narrative ... is full of interest for its real grace and\r\ndelicacy, and the exquisiteness and purity of the English in which it is\r\nwritten.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Advertiser._\r\n\r\n\r\n                         THE RECTORY CHILDREN.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn _The Rectory Children_ Mrs. Molesworth has written one of those\r\ndelightful volumes which we always look for at Christmas\r\ntime.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Athen\xc3\xa6um._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cQuiet, sunny, interesting, and thoroughly winning and\r\nwholesome.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Journal._\r\n\r\n_The Rectory Children_\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cThere is no writer of children\xe2\x80\x99s books more\r\nworthy of their admiration and love than Mrs. Molesworth. Her bright and\r\nsweet invention is so truthful, her characters so faithfully drawn, and\r\nthe teaching of her stories so tender and noble, that while they please\r\nand charm they insensibly distil into the youthful mind the most\r\nvaluable lessons. In _The Rectory Children_ we have a fresh, bright\r\nstory that will be sure to please all her young admirers.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Christian at\r\nWork._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_The Rectory Children_, by Mrs. Molesworth, is a very pretty story of\r\nEnglish life. Mrs. Molesworth is one of the most popular and charming of\r\nEnglish story-writers for children. Her child characters are true to\r\nlife, always natural and attractive, and her stories are wholesome and\r\ninteresting.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Indianapolis Journal._\r\n\r\n\r\n                                 ROSY.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Rosy_, like all the rest of her stories, is bright and pure and\r\nutterly free from cant,\xe2\x80\x94a book that children will read with pleasure and\r\nlasting profit.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Traveller._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere is no one who has a genius better adapted for entertaining\r\nchildren than Mrs. Molesworth, and her latest story, _Rosy_, is one of\r\nher best. It is illustrated with eight woodcuts from designs by Walter\r\nCrane.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Philadelphia Press._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c... Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s clever _Rosy_, a story showing in a charming way\r\nhow one little girl\xe2\x80\x99s jealousy and bad temper were conquered; one of the\r\nbest, most suggestive and improving of the Christmas juveniles.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_New\r\nYork Tribune._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Rosy_ is an exceedingly graceful and interesting story by Mrs.\r\nMolesworth, one of the best and most popular writers of juvenile\r\nfiction. This little story is full of tenderness, is fragrant in\r\nsentiment, and points with great delicacy and genuine feeling a charming\r\nmoral.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Boston Gazette._\r\n\r\n\r\n                            THE GIRLS AND I.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps the most striking feature of this pleasant story is the natural\r\nmanner in which it is written. It is just like the conversation of a\r\nbright boy\xe2\x80\x94consistently like it from beginning to end. It is a boy who\r\nis the hero of the tale, and he tells the adventures of himself and\r\nthose nearest him. He is, by the way, in many respects an example for\r\nmost young persons. It is a story characterized by sweetness and\r\npurity\xe2\x80\x94a desirable one to put into the hands of youthful\r\nreaders.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Gettysburg Monthly._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c... A delightful and purposeful story which no one can read without\r\nbeing benefited.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_New York Observer._\r\n\r\n\r\n                                 MARY.\r\n\r\n              Mrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s last story. _Just Ready._\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMrs. Molesworth\xe2\x80\x99s reputation as a writer of story-books is so well\r\nestablished that any new book of hers scarce needs a word of\r\nintroduction.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94_Home Journal._\r\n\r\n                            MACMILLAN & CO.,\r\n                       66 FIFTH AVENUE, NEW YORK.\r\n\r\n[Illustration: Book back cover.]\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                          Transcriber\xe2\x80\x99s Notes\r\n\r\n\r\n--Copyright notice provided as in the original\xe2\x80\x94this e-text is public\r\n  domain in the country of publication.\r\n\r\n--Silently corrected palpable typos;
